center;"><span style="font-size: xx-small;"><span style="font-family: sans-serif;"><a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-x-2Y3noYZtA/WbqUPBKlQBI/AAAAAAAAHDo/-gcyhcgq2IovlYBMPmLN9qb-sJY8Zs6WgCK4BGAYYCw/s1600/image-767380.png"><img alt="" border="0" height="200" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_6465643216094172658" src="reqs/1.bp.blogspot.com/-n47voh9Geo4/WbqUP6O1FfI/AAAAAAAAHDw/r5R8enwj_kUF9GWuCu28nBaarkg2355zACK4BGAYYCw/s200/image-768827.png" width="200" /></a><span style="font-family: sans-serif;"><br /></span></span></div><div style="text-align: center;"><span style="font-size: xx-small;"><br /></span></div><div style="text-align: center;"><center> <div style="text-align: justify; width: 500px;"><span style="font-size: xx-small;">In&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ancient_Greece" rel="noopener" target="_blank" title="Ancient Greece">Ancient Greece</a>, the&nbsp;<strong>Gorgoneion</strong>&nbsp;(<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greek_language" rel="noopener" target="_blank" title="Greek language">Greek</a>: Γοργόνειον) was a special&nbsp;<a class="m_-5251545944276131128gmail-m_-193030582539224673gmail-m_1549681520694793596gmail-m_697481061958925249gmail-mw-redirect" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apotropaic" rel="noopener" target="_blank" title="Apotropaic">apotropaic</a>&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amulet" rel="noopener" target="_blank" title="Amulet">amulet</a>&nbsp;show<wbr></wbr>ing the&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gorgon" rel="noopener" target="_blank" title="Gorgon">Gorgon</a>&nbsp;head, used most famously by the&nbsp;<a class="m_-5251545944276131128gmail-m_-193030582539224673gmail-m_1549681520694793596gmail-m_697481061958925249gmail-mw-redirect" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Olympian_gods" rel="noopener" target="_blank" title="Olympian gods">Olympian deities</a>&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Athena" rel="noopener" target="_blank" title="Athena">Athena</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zeus" rel="noopener" target="_blank" title="Zeus">Zeus</a>: both are said to have worn the gorgoneion as a protective&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pendant" rel="noopener" target="_blank" title="Pendant">pendant</a>.<sup class="m_-5251545944276131128gmail-m_-193030582539224673gmail-m_1549681520694793596gmail-m_697481061958925249gmail-reference" id="m_-5251545944276131128gmail-m_-193030582539224673gmail-m_1549681520694793596gmail-m_697481061958925249gmail-cite_ref-Vassilika_1-0"><a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gorgoneion#cite_note-Vassilika-1" rel="noopener" target="_blank">[1]</a></sup>&nbsp;It was assumed, among other godlike attributes, as a royal&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aegis" rel="noopener" target="_blank" title="Aegis">aegis</a>&nbsp;to imply divine birth or protection, by rulers of the&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hellenistic_period" rel="noopener" target="_blank" title="Hellenistic period">Hellenistic age</a>, as shown, for instance, on the&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_Mosaic" rel="noopener" target="_blank" title="Alexander Mosaic">Alexander Mosaic</a>&nbsp;and the&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gonzaga_Cameo" rel="noopener" target="_blank" title="Gonzaga Cameo">Gonzaga Cameo</a>.  </span><br /><div></div><div><span style="font-size: xx-small;">A&nbsp;<strong>neuralyzer</strong>, sometimes spelled as&nbsp;<strong>neuralizer</strong>, is a device seen in the&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Men_in_Black_(franchise)" rel="noopener" target="_blank" title="Men in Black (franchise)">Men in Black franchise</a>. It is one of the&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Signature_weapon" rel="noopener" target="_blank" title="Signature weapon">signature tools</a>&nbsp;and considered standard issue employed by the&nbsp;<a class="m_-5251545944276131128gmail-m_-193030582539224673gmail-m_1549681520694793596gmail-m_697481061958925249gmail-mw-redirect" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Men_in_Black" rel="noopener" target="_blank" title="Men in Black">Men in Black</a>. It is a device about the size of an average&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cigar" rel="noopener" target="_blank" title="Cigar">cigar</a>&nbsp;tube that gives a bright flash which erases the memories of the past hours, days, weeks, months or years, depending on the chosen settings. It first appeared in the first issue of the comic book series, and has appeared in all three films, as well as the&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Men_in_Black:_The_Series" rel="noopener" target="_blank" title="Men in Black: The Series">animated TV series</a>. It also has changed from red to blue.</span></div><div></div><div><div><span style="font-size: xx-small;"><strong>Apotr<a href="./HYAMDAI.html" target="_blank">op</a></strong><strong><span style='font-family: "arial black" , sans-serif;'>aic</span></strong><strong>&nbsp;magic</strong>&nbsp;(from Greek&nbsp;<em>apotrepein</em>&nbsp;"to ward off" from&nbsp;<em>apo-</em>&nbsp;"away" and&nbsp;<em>trepein</em>&nbsp;"<span style='font-family: "arial black" , sans-serif;'>to turn</span>") is a type of&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Magic_(paranormal)" rel="noopener" target="_blank" title="Magic (paranormal)">magic</a>&nbsp;intended to turn away harm or evil influences, as in deflecting misfortune or averting the&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Evil_eye" rel="noopener" target="_blank" title="Evil eye">evil eye</a>. Apotropaic observances may also be practiced out of vague&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Superstition" rel="noopener" target="_blank" title="Superstition">superstition</a>&nbsp;or out of tradition, as in&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Good_luck_charm" rel="noopener" target="_blank" title="Good luck charm">good luck charm</a>&nbsp;(perhaps some token on a&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charm_bracelet" rel="noopener" target="_blank" title="Charm bracelet">charm bracelet</a>),&nbsp;<a class="m_-5251545944276131128gmail-m_-193030582539224673gmail-m_1549681520694793596gmail-m_697481061958925249gmail-mw-redirect" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amulets" rel="noopener" target="_blank" title="Amulets">amulets</a>, or gestures such as&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crossed_fingers" rel="noopener" target="_blank" title="Crossed fingers"><span style='font-family: "arial black" , sans-serif;'>crossed fingers</span></a>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Knocking_on_wood" rel="noopener" target="_blank" title="Knocking on wood">knocking on wood</a>. The Greeks made offerings to the averting gods (Ἀποτρόπαιοι θεοί:&nbsp;<em>Apotropaioi Theoi</em>),&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chthonic" rel="noopener" target="_blank" title="Chthonic">chthonic</a>&nbsp;deities and&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hero" rel="noopener" target="_blank" title="Hero">heroes</a>&nbsp;who grant safety and deflect evil.<sup class="m_-5251545944276131128gmail-m_-193030582539224673gmail-m_1549681520694793596gmail-m_697481061958925249gmail-reference" id="m_-5251545944276131128gmail-m_-193030582539224673gmail-m_1549681520694793596gmail-m_697481061958925249gmail-cite_ref-1"><a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apotropaic_magic#cite_note-1" rel="noopener" target="_blank">[1]</a></sup></span></div><div><span style="font-size: xx-small;"><span style="font-family: sans-serif;"><br /></span> </span><br /><div><span style="font-size: xx-small;">Among the Ancient Greeks the most widely used image intended to avert evil was that of the&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gorgon" rel="noopener" target="_blank" title="Gorgon">Gorgon</a>, the head of which now may be called the&nbsp;<em><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gorgoneion" rel="noopener" target="_blank" title="Gorgoneion">Gorgoneion</a></em>, which features wild eyes, fangs, and protruding tongue. The full figure of the Gorgon holds the apex of the oldest remaining Greek temple where she is flanked by two lionesses. The Gorgon head was mounted on the&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aegis" rel="noopener" target="_blank" title="Aegis">aegis</a>&nbsp;and shield of&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Athena" rel="noopener" target="_blank" title="Athena">Athena</a>.<sup class="m_-5251545944276131128gmail-m_-193030582539224673gmail-m_1549681520694793596gmail-m_697481061958925249gmail-reference" id="m_-5251545944276131128gmail-m_-193030582539224673gmail-m_1549681520694793596gmail-m_697481061958925249gmail-cite_ref-5"><a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apotropaic_magic#cite_note-5" rel="noopener" target="_blank">[5]</a></sup></span></div><div></div><div><span style="font-size: xx-small;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eye" rel="noopener" target="_blank" title="Eye">Eyes</a>&nbsp;were often painted to ward off the&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Evil_eye" rel="noopener" target="_blank" title="Evil eye">evil eye</a>. An exaggerated apotropaic eye or a pair of eyes were painted on Greek drinking vessels called&nbsp;<em>kylikes</em>&nbsp;(<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eye-cup" rel="noopener" target="_blank" title="Eye-cup">eye-cups</a>) from the 6th century BC. The exaggerated eyes may have been intended to prevent&nbsp;<a class="m_-5251545944276131128gmail-m_-193030582539224673gmail-m_1549681520694793596gmail-m_697481061958925249gmail-mw-redirect" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Evil_spirits" rel="noopener" target="_blank" title="Evil spirits">evil spirits</a>&nbsp;from entering the mouth while drinking.<sup class="m_-5251545944276131128gmail-m_-193030582539224673gmail-m_1549681520694793596gmail-m_697481061958925249gmail-reference" id="m_-5251545944276131128gmail-m_-193030582539224673gmail-m_1549681520694793596gmail-m_697481061958925249gmail-cite_ref-6"><a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apotropaic_magic#cite_note-6" rel="noopener" target="_blank">[6]</a></sup><sup class="m_-5251545944276131128gmail-m_-193030582539224673gmail-m_1549681520694793596gmail-m_697481061958925249gmail-reference" id="m_-5251545944276131128gmail-m_-193030582539224673gmail-m_1549681520694793596gmail-m_697481061958925249gmail-cite_ref-7"><a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apotropaic_magic#cite_note-7" rel="noopener" target="_blank">[7]</a></sup>&nbsp;<a class="m_-5251545944276131128gmail-m_-193030582539224673gmail-m_1549681520694793596gmail-m_697481061958925249gmail-mw-redirect" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fishing_boat" rel="noopener" target="_blank" title="Fishing boat">Fishing boats</a>&nbsp;in some parts of the&nbsp;<a class="m_-5251545944276131128gmail-m_-193030582539224673gmail-m_1549681520694793596gmail-m_697481061958925249gmail-mw-redirect" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mediterranean" rel="noopener" target="_blank" title="Mediterranean">Mediterranean</a>&nbsp;region still have stylised eyes painted on the bows. A&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkish_people" rel="noopener" target="_blank" title="Turkish people">Turkish</a>&nbsp;<a class="m_-5251545944276131128gmail-m_-193030582539224673gmail-m_1549681520694793596gmail-m_697481061958925249gmail-mw-redirect" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Budget_airline" rel="noopener" target="_blank" title="Budget airline">budget airline</a>,&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fly_Air" rel="noopener" target="_blank" title="Fly Air">Fly Havayolu Taşımacılık A.Ş.</a>, had adopted the symbol (known as&nbsp;<em><a class="m_-5251545944276131128gmail-m_-193030582539224673gmail-m_1549681520694793596gmail-m_697481061958925249gmail-mw-redirect" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nazar_boncu%C4%9Fu" rel="noopener" target="_blank" title="Nazar boncuğu">Nazar boncuğu</a></em>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<em>Nazar bonjuk</em>) as a motif for the&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vertical_stabilizer" rel="noopener" target="_blank" title="Vertical stabilizer">vertical stabilizer</a>&nbsp;of its aeroplanes. The Yiddish expression,&nbsp;<em>Kain ein horeh</em>&nbsp;(<span class="m_-5251545944276131128gmail-m_-193030582539224673gmail-m_1549681520694793596gmail-m_697481061958925249gmail-script-hebrew" dir="rtl">קיין עין הרע</span>‎) is apotropaic in nature, and literally translates to "<span style='font-family: "arial black" , sans-serif;'>no evil eye</span>", somewhat equivalent to the expression, "<a class="m_-5251545944276131128gmail-m_-193030582539224673gmail-m_1549681520694793596gmail-m_697481061958925249gmail-mw-redirect" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Knock_on_wood" rel="noopener" target="_blank" title="Knock on wood"><span style='font-family: "arial black" , sans-serif;'>Knock on wood</span></a>."</span></div></div><div></div><div><span style="font-size: xx-small;">Changes to the neuralyzer have been featured in the films. In the&nbsp;<a class="m_-5251545944276131128gmail-m_-193030582539224673gmail-m_1549681520694793596gmail-m_697481061958925249gmail-mw-redirect" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Men_in_Black_(film)" rel="noopener" target="_blank" title="Men in Black (film)">first movie</a>, the color of its eye was red. This was later changed to blue in the&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Men_in_Black_II" rel="noopener" target="_blank" title="Men in Black II">second film</a>. It remains blue in the&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Men_in_Black_3" rel="noopener" target="_blank" title="Men in Black 3">third film</a>, although the shade is more of a turquoise rather than the previous film's aqua, and the design of the neuralyzer itself is considerably different compared to the previous films. In the first movie, Agent J calls the neuralyzer the "flashy thing" and dislikes the idea of using it and when he has to use it, believes that they should supply the victims with the best memories possible rather than Agent K's mundane and depressing memories. He used it at the end of the movie on K, wiping out 35 years of his service using the neuralyzer.</span></div><div></div><div><div class="m_-5251545944276131128gmail-m_-193030582539224673gmail-m_1549681520694793596gmail-m_697481061958925249gmail-g"><div><div class="m_-5251545944276131128gmail-m_-193030582539224673gmail-m_1549681520694793596gmail-m_697481061958925249gmail-rc"><div class="m_-5251545944276131128gmail-m_-193030582539224673gmail-m_1549681520694793596gmail-m_697481061958925249gmail-s"><div class="m_-5251545944276131128gmail-m_-193030582539224673gmail-m_1549681520694793596gmail-m_697481061958925249gmail-f m_-5251545944276131128gmail-m_-193030582539224673gmail-m_1549681520694793596gmail-m_697481061958925249gmail-kv m_-5251545944276131128gmail-m_-193030582539224673gmail-m_1549681520694793596gmail-m_697481061958925249gmail-_SWb"><cite class="m_-5251545944276131128gmail-m_-193030582539224673gmail-m_1549681520694793596gmail-m_697481061958925249gmail-_Rm m_-5251545944276131128gmail-m_-193030582539224673gmail-m_1549681520694793596gmail-m_697481061958925249gmail-bc"><span style="font-size: xx-small;"><a href="https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/" rel="noopener" target="_blank">https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov</a>&nbsp;› NCBI › Literature › PubMed Central (PMC)</span></cite></div><div class="m_-5251545944276131128gmail-m_-193030582539224673gmail-m_1549681520694793596gmail-m_697481061958925249gmail-slp m_-5251545944276131128gmail-m_-193030582539224673gmail-m_1549681520694793596gmail-m_697481061958925249gmail-f"><span style="font-size: xx-small;">by JD Bremner - ‎2006 - ‎<a class="m_-5251545944276131128gmail-m_-193030582539224673gmail-m_1549681520694793596gmail-m_697481061958925249gmail-fl" href="http://scholar.google.com/scholar?rlz=1CAACAR_enUS749US749&amp;um=1&amp;ie=UTF-8&amp;lr&amp;cites=6031977196911932210" rel="noopener" target="_blank">Cited by 218</a>&nbsp;- ‎<a class="m_-5251545944276131128gmail-m_-193030582539224673gmail-m_1549681520694793596gmail-m_697481061958925249gmail-fl" href="http://scholar.google.com/scholar?rlz=1CAACAR_enUS749US749&amp;um=1&amp;ie=UTF-8&amp;lr&amp;q=related:MjMxQ03jtVP6wM:scholar.google.com/" rel="noopener" target="_blank">Related articles</a></span></div><span class="m_-5251545944276131128gmail-m_-193030582539224673gmail-m_1549681520694793596gmail-m_697481061958925249gmail-st"><span style="font-size: xx-small;">Brain areas implicated in the stress response include the amygdala, hippocampus, and prefrontal cortex. ... They also play a critical role in&nbsp;memory, highlighting the important interplay between&nbsp;memory&nbsp;and thetraumatic&nbsp;stress response. Preclinical&nbsp;studies&nbsp;show that stress affects these brain areas.</span></span></div><div According to the books of&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Book_of_Exodus" style='background: transparent; color: rgb(37 , 161 , 134); font-family: "arial" , sans-serif;' target="_blank" title="Book of Exodus">Exodus</a>,&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Book_of_Numbers" style='background: transparent; font-size: xx-small;'>According to the second chapter of Genesis, Eve was created by&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/God_in_Abrahamic_religions" style='background: transparent; color: rgb(37 , 161 , 134); font-family: "arial" , sans-serif;' target="_blank" title="God in Abrahamic religions">God</a>&nbsp;(<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yahweh" style='background: transparent; color: rgb(37 , 161 , 134); font-family: "arial" , sans-serif;' target="_blank" title="Yahweh">Yahweh</a>) by taking her from the rib<span class="m_-5251545944276131128gmail-m_-193030582539224673gmail-m_1549681520694793596gmail-m_-2406931458228765498m_7062753601417727326gmail-m_258112447631369337m_2341308960067590409m_4521999671932699583gmail-m_-6182954198820330264gmail-m_521289457461777515m_1359743985997052155m_2062399313490225364m_7360525420591546646gmail-m_-2943162030376724839m_4715356690998560955gmail-m_-7537480698924484776m_-278294240238056367gmail-m_-5546344077922119487gmail-m_3924190074418593144gmail-m_201252411975995256gmail-reference" id="m_-5251545944276131128gmail-m_-193030582539224673gmail-m_1549681520694793596gmail-m_-2406931458228765498m_7062753601417727326gmail-m_258112447631369337m_2341308960067590409m_4521999671932699583gmail-m_-6182954198820330264gmail-m_521289457461777515m_1359743985997052155m_2062399313490225364m_7360525420591546646gmail-m_-2943162030376724839m_4715356690998560955gmail-m_-7537480698924484776m_-278294240238056367gmail-m_-5546344077922119487gmail-m_3924190074418593144gmail-m_201252411975995256gmail-cite_ref-2" style="font-size: 6.75px; line-height: 0; vertical-align: baseline;"><a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eve#cite_note-2" style='background: transparent; color: rgb(37 , 161 , 134); font-family: "arial" , sans-serif;' target="_blank">[2]</a></span>&nbsp;of&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adam" style='background: transparent; color: rgb(37 , 161 , 134); font-family: "arial" , sans-serif;' target="_blank" title="Adam">Adam</a>, to be Adam's companion. She succumbs to the&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Serpent_(symbolism)" style='background: transparent; color: rgb(37 , 161 , 134); font-family: "arial" , sans-serif;' target="_blank" title="Serpent (symbolism)">serpent</a>'s temptation to eat the&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Forbidden_fruit" style='background: transparent; color: rgb(37 , 161 , 134); font-family: "arial" , sans-serif;' target="_blank" title="Forbidden fruit">forbidden fruit</a>&nbsp;from the&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tree_of_the_knowledge_of_good_and_evil" style='background: transparent; color: rgb(37 , 161 , 134); font-family: "arial" , sans-serif;' target="_blank" title="Tree of the knowledge of good and evil">tree of the knowledge of good and evil</a>. She shares the fruit with Adam, and as a result the first humans are expelled from the&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Garden_of_Eden" style='background: transparent; color: rgb(37 , 161 , 134); font-family: "arial" , sans-serif;' target="_blank" title="Garden of Eden">Garden of Eden</a>. Christian churches differ on how they view both Adam and Eve's disobedience to God (often called the&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fall_of_man" style='background: transparent; color: rgb(37 , 161 , 134); font-family: "arial" , sans-serif;' target="_blank" title="Fall of man">fall of man</a>), and to the consequences that those actions had on the rest of humanity. Christian and Jewish teachings sometimes hold&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adam" style='background: transparent; color: rgb(37 , 161 , 134); font-family: "arial" , sans-serif;' target="_blank" title="Adam">Adam</a>&nbsp;(the first man) and Eve to a different level of responsibility for the fall, although&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islam" style='background: transparent; color: rgb(37 , 161 , 134); font-family: "arial" , sans-serif;' target="_blank" title="Islam">Islamic</a>&nbsp;teaching holds both equally responsible.</span><br /><span style='font-family: "lora" , serif; font-size: xx-small;'><br /></span><span style='font-family: "lora" , serif; font-size: xx-small;'>Although Eve is not a saint's name, the traditional&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Name_day" style='background: transparent; color: rgb(37 , 161 , 134); font-family: "arial" , sans-serif;' target="_blank" title="Name day">name day</a>&nbsp;of&nbsp;<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adam_and_Eve" style='background: transparent; color: rgb(37 , 161 , 134); font-family: "arial" , sans-serif;' target="_blank" title="Adam and Eve">Adam and Eve</a>&nbsp;has been celebrated on December 24</span><br /><span style="font-family: arial black, sans-serif; font-size: xx-small;"><br />From&nbsp;<span color: rgb(37 , 161 , 134); font-family: "lora" , serif; font-size: 20px;' target="_blank" title="Israelites">Israelites</a><span style='font-family: "lora" , serif; font-size: 20px;'>&nbsp;in the&nbsp;</span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hebrew_Bible" style='background: transparent; color: rgb(37 , 161 , 134); font-family: "lora" , serif; font-size: 20px;' target="_blank" title="Hebrew Bible">Hebrew Bible</a><span style='font-family: "lora" , serif; font-size: 20px;'>.&nbsp;</span><em style="font-family: Lora,serif; font-size: 20px;"><span lang="he-Latn"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/El_(deity)" style='background: transparent; color: rgb(37 , 161 , 134); font-family: "arial" , sans-serif;' target="_blank" title="El (deity)">ʾĒl</a>&nbsp;ʿElyōn</span></em><span style='font-family: "lora" , serif; font-size: 20px;'>&nbsp;is usually rendered in English as "God Most High", and similarly in the Septuagint as "Ο ΘΕΟΣ Ο ΥΨΙΣΤΟΣ" ("God the highest").</span></div></div></center></div><div style="font-family: Lora,serif;
